  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_f32a0d2c-045e-4a44-a762-93f2b79dc071'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

<div id="review_1494286827" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1494286827" />
    <a title="Jack Tripper" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/35473855-jack-tripper"><img alt="Jack Tripper" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1484547420p2/35473855.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1494286827?book_show_action=true">Jan 03, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jack Tripper" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jack Tripper" href="/user/show/35473855-jack-tripper">Jack Tripper</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35473855-jack-tripper?shelf=weird">weird</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35473855-jack-tripper?shelf=graphic-novel">graphic-novel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35473855-jack-tripper?shelf=translation">translation</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35473855-jack-tripper?shelf=slice-of-life">slice-of-life</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1494286827" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15092763932807293262"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1458529658i/18497872._SX540_.png' width='500' height='345' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I actually know little to nothing about manga, other than having read Ito's <i>Uzumaki</i> and a few issues of <i>Akira</i> back in the day. But just over a year ago I came across an online article proclaiming Inio Asano's <i>Nijigahara Holograph</i> one of the ten best graphic novels of 2014, comparing the sinister, dreamlike atmosphere to a David Lynch film. So of course I immediately bought and read it, and was totally enveloped the entire time. It wasn't just one of the best graphic novels I'd ever read, it was </span>
  <span id="freeText15092763932807293262" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1458529658i/18497872._SX540_.png" width="500" height="345" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I actually know little to nothing about manga, other than having read Ito's <i>Uzumaki</i> and a few issues of <i>Akira</i> back in the day. But just over a year ago I came across an online article proclaiming Inio Asano's <i>Nijigahara Holograph</i> one of the ten best graphic novels of 2014, comparing the sinister, dreamlike atmosphere to a David Lynch film. So of course I immediately bought and read it, and was totally enveloped the entire time. It wasn't just one of the best graphic novels I'd ever read, it was one of the best and most powerful pieces of storytelling I'd ever experienced, in any medium. I immediately snatched up everything else by Asano that was available in English (which wasn't much), and while I enjoyed them, mostly they were normal "slice of life," love and heartbreak-type stuff. Which is fine, but I really missed the weirdness of <i>Nijigahara</i>. <i>Punpun</i> seemed right up my alley, a mixture of "slice of life" and the bizarre, but it was still only available in Japanese. After searching for any online, fan-made translations to no avail, then (briefly) considering learning Japanese, I decided to wait til it was made available in English.<br><br>Now that it's here, I can say it was definitely worth the wait. The artwork is absolutely stunning, and while the story didn't grab me <i>quite</i> as much as <i>Nijigahara</i>, it was still pretty damn absorbing, and this is only the very beginning of an epic story spanning several years, tracing Punpun's life from an adolescent to an adult. This first volume follows Punpun's years in grade school (or the Japanese equivalent of it), dealing with his parents' divorce, succumbing to things like peer pressure and love, and dreaming of one day colonizing distant planets (as he thinks this will impress the new girl in town, whom he loves). He sees himself as an outsider, not really belonging anywhere, which I suppose is why he's drawn like a cartoonish bird while everyone and everything else is more lifelike. <br><br>But it's not just a coming of age story, as there are Murakami-esque moments where unreality and reality collide, such as when Punpun repeats a simple chant that his hip, slacker uncle taught him for when he needs God to show up and help. I won't tell you what God is like, but it's pretty hilarious and tripped-out. We also see that one of his buddies has an entirely different God that appears for him. And Punpun's thoughts and daydreams are pretty hallucinogenic as well.<br><br>Most importantly, Asano is a master at depicting the joys and triumphs, as well as the anxieties and tragedies, of growing up. He is able to make the simplest, most everyday accomplishments seem like a massive feat, which is of course true when you're 9 or 10, and it was true for me while reading. The weirdness that creeps in occasionally doesn't feel out of place at all in this otherwise pretty realistic (sometimes gut-wrenchingly realistic) story. It's a near-perfect marriage of "boy meets world"-type stories and otherworldly strangeness, and I'm already counting down the days until volume 2 becomes available.<br><br>Recommended to pretty much everybody who's looking for a moving, first-class coming of age story. As long as you don't mind a side of straight-up weird to go along with it.<br><br>4.5 Stars,<br><br>or<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1458538406i/18498308._SX540_.png" width="500" height="345" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="15092763932807293262" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2328019616" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2328019616" />
    <a title="A Wary Reader" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/46727197-a-wary-reader"><img alt="A Wary Reader" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1555655408p2/46727197.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2328019616?book_show_action=true">Mar 14, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="A Wary Reader" class="user" itemprop="url" name="A Wary Reader" href="/user/show/46727197-a-wary-reader">A Wary Reader</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2328019616" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1862046123829526745"><i>“Happiness describes moments, and it's never permanent."</i><br/><br/>"This manga has officially ruined and saved my life." is what I told my friend years ago when I finished Goodnight Punpun. I don't think I'll be able to properly convey my feelings for this story in a review today. I can write an entire essay, but it won’t be enough for me to describe how this manga changed the little fourteen year old me, and how close I keep it to my heart even now. <br/><br/>Goodnight Punpun centres around Punpun, an idealist and </span>
  <span id="freeText1862046123829526745" style="display:none"><i>“Happiness describes moments, and it's never permanent."</i><br /><br />"This manga has officially ruined and saved my life." is what I told my friend years ago when I finished Goodnight Punpun. I don't think I'll be able to properly convey my feelings for this story in a review today. I can write an entire essay, but it won’t be enough for me to describe how this manga changed the little fourteen year old me, and how close I keep it to my heart even now. <br /><br />Goodnight Punpun centres around Punpun, an idealist and a hopeless romantic depicted as a little caricatured bird throughout the most of the series. The tale follows his life and the people around him, his transition into adulthood and his love life. On the surface, it sounds like a cute, simple coming-of-age story, but so much unfolds in these pages I no longer see it in such way. This manga was crafted to be difficult to comprehend, there are themes in this story that make it so deliciously bizarre. <br /><br />Without a doubt, this is one of the most enthralling manga series I’ve read. I’ve seen stories that attempt to capture the hardships and struggles of life, but Asano goes far beyond that in Goodnight Punpun. It’s not a story that’ll appeal to everyone, the idea of it is abstract and peculiar to some people, but I know others, including myself, were absolutely astonished by this manga. It is impactful, heartbreaking, beautiful, and it will shape you as a person, as it did with me. <br /><br />Of course, the delivery of the story wouldn’t have been as effective if it weren’t for Asano’s art style. Everything in Goodnight Punpun is beautifully drawn, I remember flipping through the pages and marvelling at how impossibly realistic the characters and the settings looked. The illustrations reflect the atmosphere of the manga, it’s compelling and mesmerising, and conveys the emotions of the characters well across the panels. Inio Asano has some of the most impressive and unique artistic skills I’ve seen, in his other works, but shines much brighter in the later volumes of the series. <br /><br />This is a manga that made me think, but most importantly, it made the my cold, empty heart feel. Yes, it made me ponder about adolescence, about youth, it made me think about identity and the complexity of people, but it made me feel so intensely for the protagonist and the characters surrounding him. I was frustrated with Punpun. His decisions and choices in life are unethical, and utterly terrible at times, but there were moments I understood these flaws made him so very pitiful, and so very human. A poignant reminder that I, along with everyone else in the world, could be exactly like Punpun at our lowest point in life. <br /><br />Goodnight Punpun is a masterpiece. I highly recommend this manga to everyone, unless you suffer from severe depression, because this story isn’t the happiest one out there. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[It does involve vivid depictions of suicide, abuse, rape, etc. It's not for the faint-hearted readers. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> It's a solid 5/5 for me. <br /><br />I'll just end it here with another favourite quote of mine in the series: <br /><br /><i>“…If we see shooting stars, what would you wish for, Punpun?”<br />“Wishing upon shooting stars doesn’t make them come true.”<br />“Right, but what if. What would you wish if they did…?”<br />“I’d wish for shooting stars to disappear forever.”</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="1862046123829526745" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer10785236466929702130">This is the first big omnibus collection of Asano's tale of a little chicken-like creature, Punpun, his dysfunctional family, friends, and his crush on a girl. This is basically a coming of age story and the tone of it is much like his also accomplished Solanin, somewhat subdued, but with fantasy/magical realism thrown in. It's funny and sweet, for the most part. I might have liked it more had I not had Asano's amazing and much darker Nijigahara Holograph to compare it to, but this guy can draw!</span>
  <span id="freeText10785236466929702130" style="display:none">This is the first big omnibus collection of Asano's tale of a little chicken-like creature, Punpun, his dysfunctional family, friends, and his crush on a girl. This is basically a coming of age story and the tone of it is much like his also accomplished Solanin, somewhat subdued, but with fantasy/magical realism thrown in. It's funny and sweet, for the most part. I might have liked it more had I not had Asano's amazing and much darker Nijigahara Holograph to compare it to, but this guy can draw! The art in this one is better than the story, though this one is more accessible and more deliberately coherent (considering its younger audience, YA) than Nijigahara Holograph.</span>

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review3210747655">

<div id="review_1607774165" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1607774165" />
    <a title="Mark Schlatter" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3088726-mark-schlatter"><img alt="Mark Schlatter" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1457718316p2/3088726.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1607774165?book_show_action=true">Apr 11, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mark Schlatter" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mark Schlatter" href="/user/show/3088726-mark-schlatter">Mark Schlatter</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3088726-mark-schlatter?shelf=own">own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1607774165" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17855035982260022608">It's been a couple of days, but I'm still unsure about this book. I was a fan of Inio Asano's <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3430763.Solanin' title='Solanin by Inio Asano' rel='nofollow noopener'>Solanin</a>, a story about twenty-somethings looking for identity, but did not like <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17306314.Nijigahara_Holograph' title='Nijigahara Holograph by Inio Asano' rel='nofollow noopener'>Nijigahara Holograph</a>, a work of surreal psychological horror that I never connected to. <br/><br/>This volume has the trick/gimmick/mechanic of using a stick figure bird as our protagonist Punpun, while most of the other characters and all of the settings are fairly realistic and at times quite detailed. It looks like an application o</span>
  <span id="freeText17855035982260022608" style="display:none">It's been a couple of days, but I'm still unsure about this book. I was a fan of Inio Asano's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3430763.Solanin" title="Solanin by Inio Asano" rel="nofollow noopener">Solanin</a>, a story about twenty-somethings looking for identity, but did not like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17306314.Nijigahara_Holograph" title="Nijigahara Holograph by Inio Asano" rel="nofollow noopener">Nijigahara Holograph</a>, a work of surreal psychological horror that I never connected to. <br /><br />This volume has the trick/gimmick/mechanic of using a stick figure bird as our protagonist Punpun, while most of the other characters and all of the settings are fairly realistic and at times quite detailed. It looks like an application of the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Masking_(illustration)" rel="nofollow noopener">masking effect</a> Scott McCloud describes in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/102920.Understanding_Comics_The_Invisible_Art" title="Understanding Comics The Invisible Art by Scott McCloud" rel="nofollow noopener">Understanding Comics</a> --- you increase identification with your character because it is so easy to project yourself onto a relatively blank slate. And, to an extent, Punpun represents a typical child going to middle school, having a crush on a classmate, and dealing with lousy family dynamics.<br /><br />And yet, that "everyman" experience is mitigated, first off, because Punpun and his friends represent an exclusively heterosexual male prespective, exemplified by their search for discarded porn. Secondly, all of Punpun's relatives (his father, mother, and uncle on his mother's side) are also depicted as stick figure birds. (At times, Asano carries out the disturbing spectacle of representing the uncle as a stick figure but with realistic eyes.) And thirdly, but perhaps most importantly, the other characters and narrative regularly verge into the strange. It's tough to see an everyman story when things regularly get psychedelic. <br /><br />Some of Asano's surrealism is focused on Punpun's internal life. Punpun regularly invokes God through a nonsense prayer and sees a young man with an afro who gives questionable advice. There is a dream sequence (around the time Punpun starts masturbating) with dancing vaginas. And many times, it is clear Punpun is retreating into a visually rich mental world in order to avoid the anxiety of his life.<br /><br />But a lot of the surrealism is just out in the open. Practically every adult outside of Punpun's family is depicted as insane, from the principal and teacher at his school who play hide and seek to the family lawyer who just goes "Yup yup" all the time like a large friendly dog. And the narrative moves strangely as well, sometimes focusing on regular school life, but detouring for quite some time to a dangerous mission to an abandoned warehouse where dead bodies may have been stored.<br /><br />When the focus is on characterization, I really like the book. Asano clearly gets across Punpun's uncertainty as his family breaks apart, and I thought his friends were fascinating to read about. But I'm not sure what the sweep of the story is besides Punpun's crush, and the surrealistic bits, while expertly carried out, left me groundless.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17855035982260022608" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2366683363" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2366683363" />
    <a title="James DeSantis" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16060275-james-desantis"><img alt="James DeSantis" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604143880p2/16060275.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2366683363?book_show_action=true">Jul 15, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="James DeSantis" class="user" itemprop="url" name="James DeSantis" href="/user/show/16060275-james-desantis">James DeSantis</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2366683363" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5895984202154757723">This was...well it was weird as shit yet I read all 300+ pages in one sitting. <br/><br/>So Punpun is this ghost looking creature. His whole family actually looks like these things. However, everyone in the world is normal looking humans. It's not said if everyone else sees Punpun and his family different but I doubt it since they all act normal around them. So this is mostly in Punpun's head, and let me tell you...This is not a kids story despite 90% of it being about kids. Kids go through some crazy shi</span>
  <span id="freeText5895984202154757723" style="display:none">This was...well it was weird as shit yet I read all 300+ pages in one sitting. <br /><br />So Punpun is this ghost looking creature. His whole family actually looks like these things. However, everyone in the world is normal looking humans. It's not said if everyone else sees Punpun and his family different but I doubt it since they all act normal around them. So this is mostly in Punpun's head, and let me tell you...This is not a kids story despite 90% of it being about kids. Kids go through some crazy shit. After the first chapter ends with someone ending up in the hospital we get to see Punpun's life change by meeting a girl, exploring sex stuff with his buddies, and learning about life problems getting older. <br /><br />Good: This is a coming in age story wrapped up in some comedy and drama and weirdness and it works for the most part. The characters all feel real and different, the pacing is well done and never boring, and the subject matter is important. I also thought the designs and art are top notch. <br /><br />Bad: I think some of the weirdness is TOO much and TOO over the top at times to ruin the atmosphere sadly. I also think some of the dialog bubbles sometimes hard to read. <br /><br />Overall a interesting look into the life of a young boy and his buddies. I can't say this is a classic yet but I'm having a feeling if this series keeps up this will be. A 4 out of 5. </span>
  <a data-text-id="5895984202154757723" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer13226909283292534101">• i wasnt expecting to like the story but i did. there were weird things happening, some of which i do not understand. either that part is not related to the actual story but was included to the story itself. those left me confused but once everything goes back to normal, all was good again.<br/><br/>• this the perfect example of adults not thinking about how their actions will affect their kids. i hated punpun's mom. such a selfish human being. things certainly aren't always at it seems with the characte</span>

<div id="review_1463602562" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1463602562" />
    <a title="Silence" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5725925-silence"><img alt="Silence" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1568828188p2/5725925.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1463602562?book_show_action=true">Dec 08, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Silence" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Silence" href="/user/show/5725925-silence">Silence</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5725925-silence?shelf=manga">manga</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5725925-silence?shelf=arcs">arcs</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1463602562" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12869167492566123765">I wasn’t sure what to expect when I snagged an ARC of “Goodnight Punpun”. I mean, the publisher describes him as a kid whose life goals include wining the Nobel Prize, running away in the name of love, and finding porn. I knew it would either be the best thing ever, or the worst. It’s the best thing ever. I find it hard to explain exactly why I loved this so much. Nothing exceptional happens. It is a story about a regular boy, in a regular town, doing regular things. It should be boring, but it’</span>
  <span id="freeText12869167492566123765" style="display:none">I wasn’t sure what to expect when I snagged an ARC of “Goodnight Punpun”. I mean, the publisher describes him as a kid whose life goals include wining the Nobel Prize, running away in the name of love, and finding porn. I knew it would either be the best thing ever, or the worst. It’s the best thing ever. I find it hard to explain exactly why I loved this so much. Nothing exceptional happens. It is a story about a regular boy, in a regular town, doing regular things. It should be boring, but it’s… magical. Inio Asano has managed to take the ordinary and transform it into one of the most honest and true depictions of adolescence that I have ever seen in a manga. All those awkward moments and learning curves that most shy away from are all there. It feels as if Asano has lain all of our childhood experiences before us. Good, bad, and ugly, everyone has been through a lot of what Punpun has, and that makes him more than just a character. He is personable and real. Punpun doesn’t read like fiction, he reads like a friend you grew up with. You will root for him. You will want this kid to make it. <br /><br />The moments in Punpun’s life (a fair mix of awkward and humorous experiences) are heightened by Asano’s illustrations. His style shows such attention to detail that the final result is simply breathtaking. I adore the way he imbeds the surreal, birdlike personifications of Punpun and his family within a world that is much more true to life. The effect goes a long way towards supporting his feelings of being both and outsider and a dreamer. Overall, “Goodnight Punpun” is a game changer. I have the utmost respect for Asano as a mangaka after reading this, because it couldn’t have been easy to create. It takes a certain amount of openness and confidence in yourself to even consider breaking away from industry standards in general. To boldly lay out all those tender and perplexing things that we often goes through as we age brings that challenge to a whole new level of bravery. Inio Asano is pushing the boundaries of what manga can and should be, and for that, I salute him. <br /><br />I would like to thank Edelweiss and the publisher for providing me with a free ARC in exchange for a fair and honest review*</span>
  <a data-text-id="12869167492566123765" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer10363284490104494762">I'm a lazy man, so I'm just going to review the series as a whole, rather than try and untangle where the plot threads landed in each book. I think it's a series that should be read start to finish anyway. <br/><br/>That said, I'm not sure how accurately I can convey just what a punch to the stomach this series was. I'd say the first book is the most generally relatable, with it being a mostly standard coming of age story, albeit in the context of a very dysfunctional family. From there the reader can onl</span>
  <span id="freeText10363284490104494762" style="display:none">I'm a lazy man, so I'm just going to review the series as a whole, rather than try and untangle where the plot threads landed in each book. I think it's a series that should be read start to finish anyway. <br /><br />That said, I'm not sure how accurately I can convey just what a punch to the stomach this series was. I'd say the first book is the most generally relatable, with it being a mostly standard coming of age story, albeit in the context of a very dysfunctional family. From there the reader can only watch as the characters' lives spiral off in different directions, be it for better or worse, with paths crossing occasionally along the way. As an outside observer to it all, you are treated with an insight into how various life events stack one on top of the other, creating a mound of insecurities in the shape of a little bird thing. After following Punpun from grade school to his early 20s, everything culminates in one of the most gut wrenching finales in any piece of media I have consumed. I won't say I'm happy after reading this, but I will say I am extremely glad I did.<br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_1775384534" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1775384534" />
    <a title="Terrence" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/58156435-terrence"><img alt="Terrence" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1472360881p2/58156435.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1775384534?book_show_action=true">Oct 22, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Terrence" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Terrence" href="/user/show/58156435-terrence">Terrence</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/58156435-terrence?shelf=z-goodreads-finds">z-goodreads-finds</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1775384534" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8857472266679595974">WHAT?! I think that word sums up this manga.<br/><br/>Punpun is about an innocent pigeon boy (in a class of human students) learning about the bees and the birds, life, and whatever else there is to know. How he remained so innocent in this world is anybody's guess.<br/><br/>This is a really creepy book compared to some of Asano's other works that I've read, and certainly geared towards an older audience (repeat, this is not for anyone under the age of 18 despite the cute looking anthropomorphic main character). Wh</span>
  <span id="freeText8857472266679595974" style="display:none">WHAT?! I think that word sums up this manga.<br /><br />Punpun is about an innocent pigeon boy (in a class of human students) learning about the bees and the birds, life, and whatever else there is to know. How he remained so innocent in this world is anybody's guess.<br /><br />This is a really creepy book compared to some of Asano's other works that I've read, and certainly geared towards an older audience (repeat, this is not for anyone under the age of 18 despite the cute looking anthropomorphic main character). While Nijigahara had bouts of insanity, it was still packaged in a generally normal plot. Solanin was basically entirely realistic, with dreams being the only opportunity for Asano to go crazy. This on the other hand has something as wacky as Asano's caricature size head coming down to talk to the main character and observe him as a god. Sexual themes abound. Punpun's mother gets beaten by his father in the opening chapter, so he goes to jail, she goes into silence at the hospital from PTSD, and Punpun has to live with his Uncle, Yuichi. A lot of the adult human characters also look insane, like smaller versions of the Attack on Titan collosi. It's just extremely chaotic. <br /><br />You can't help but think of something like Southpark while reading this since you have that same mix of adult attitudes and humor in a school setting for contrast. This is best seen in Aiko, Punpun's love interest, a gap toothed girl who talks about the end of the world due to an oil shortage, and how we have to get off the planet; until then she plans to blow all her money as a teen because the end is nigh if we don't find an interplanetary solution before she becomes an adult. <br /><br />You'll laugh, you'll cringe, and you'll cry at the content in this book. It's a very sensory experience. Much like Solanin, Punpun lets its dialogue do the talking, many panels broken up by three panels with just words over a black background. These are usually poignant messages that seem to go beyond the plot itself, to reach out to the reader and others on the subjects of tough and confusing times in life. Punpun also has moments where his expression does the talking as well. <br /><br />I've kind of been looking for something off kilter, non traditional, and... I guess I found it. It's almost too bizarre, but I won't knock points for that. The art is amazing by the way, whether you ignore or inclufe the weird imagery. I'd say it's better than Solanin and Nijigahara, which is weird to say considering this features a nondescript looking stick figure bird as the protagonist. </span>
  <a data-text-id="8857472266679595974" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review1775384534">

<div id="review_1872544902" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1872544902" />
    <a title="Alexa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/38943910-alexa"><img alt="Alexa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1431625226p2/38943910.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1872544902?book_show_action=true">Jan 11, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alexa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alexa" href="/user/show/38943910-alexa">Alexa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38943910-alexa?shelf=comics-manga-graphic-novels">comics-manga-graphic-novels</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1872544902" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10203718763461731775">This story is reminiscent of what it really feels like to be a kid. As an adult I've grown cynical and jaded, but Punpun renews this sense of innocence in me. It's amazing to me to be reminded of all the things I once found so unbelievably important to myself, and how since the timeline of my life has stretched so has my depth of understanding of what may be deemed as 'important.' <br/><br/>The naïveté of Punpun is touching, and it garners an empathy from within me, allowing me to reevaluate what I hold d</span>
  <span id="freeText10203718763461731775" style="display:none">This story is reminiscent of what it really feels like to be a kid. As an adult I've grown cynical and jaded, but Punpun renews this sense of innocence in me. It's amazing to me to be reminded of all the things I once found so unbelievably important to myself, and how since the timeline of my life has stretched so has my depth of understanding of what may be deemed as 'important.' <br /><br />The naïveté of Punpun is touching, and it garners an empathy from within me, allowing me to reevaluate what I hold dear and what I choose to bottle up and ignore. <br /><br />Being an adult is complex in that we gain responsibility and an overwhelming amount of things we have to evaluate, inevitably leaving bits behind. But Punpun reminds me of how complex childhood was as well, with regards to the amplification of the importance of events because of our lack of responsibility and understanding of the world.<br /><br />We tend to forget these feelings we once held so dear, shrugging them off as poor judgment and childish whimsy, but being reminded of them and reevaluating the sheer weight of these feelings I've once held is making me feel as though they never quite lost their weight at all.<br /><br />We change and develop over time, but the stages of our personalities are encapsulated in these feelings isolated in the periods of time we once held them. Those same feelings may not be important in present day context when filtered through our current personality, but one cannot lose sight of those personalities we once embodied and the weight of the feelings that came along with them. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10203718763461731775" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2110255379" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2110255379" />
    <a title="Caroline" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/38672507-caroline"><img alt="Caroline" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1474291977p2/38672507.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2110255379?book_show_action=true">Nov 19, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Caroline" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Caroline" href="/user/show/38672507-caroline">Caroline</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38672507-caroline?shelf=graphic-novels-manga-comics">graphic-novels-manga-comics</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2110255379" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5328094990963783077">THIS was a really interesting manga. It follows Punpun Punyama who is in middle school (I think) and struggling with a number of things- his parents are having serious marital troubles, he has a crush at school, he wants to win a Nobel Prize, he isn't entirely sure there is a God, his wacky unemployed uncle comes to live with them, he wants to find some porn to watch.<br/><br/>Reading this was fun. I loved the art style! Punpun is drawn as the little bird thing we see on the cover and it's an excellent ar</span>
  <span id="freeText5328094990963783077" style="display:none">THIS was a really interesting manga. It follows Punpun Punyama who is in middle school (I think) and struggling with a number of things- his parents are having serious marital troubles, he has a crush at school, he wants to win a Nobel Prize, he isn't entirely sure there is a God, his wacky unemployed uncle comes to live with them, he wants to find some porn to watch.<br /><br />Reading this was fun. I loved the art style! Punpun is drawn as the little bird thing we see on the cover and it's an excellent artistic choice because it highlights how much of an outsider he feels like in his life whilst also being incredibly cute and charming. There were some panels and spreads in this book that were absolutely STUNNING and took my breath away!!<br /><br />I'm looking forward to pursuing this series. My rating is maybe a little closer to a <b>3.5 out of 5 stars</b> because it didn't hook me completely but I am intrigued. I loved that although it was a slice of life story it had something Murakami-esque to it, there were some bizarre and unexplainable moments in the story that I really enjoyed. Keen to read the next volume and see how Punpun grows!</span>
  <a data-text-id="5328094990963783077" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1592460382?book_show_action=true">Mar 27, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Derek Royal" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Derek Royal" href="/user/show/3060930-derek-royal">Derek Royal</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1592460382" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7541022418755521800">Reread 11/21/2016, in prep for next volumes.<br/><br/>3/27/2016 - I love Inio Asano's work, and there are many facets to his storytelling abilities. And this first volume of Goodnight Punpun is yet another side of Asano that we haven't really seen in his previous English-language releases. While the subject matter of this series isn't that different from young-protagonist-growing-up scenarios we find in Solanin and A Girl on the Shore, the tone is much more humorous, and explicitly so. The fact that the t</span>
  <span id="freeText7541022418755521800" style="display:none">Reread 11/21/2016, in prep for next volumes.<br /><br />3/27/2016 - I love Inio Asano's work, and there are many facets to his storytelling abilities. And this first volume of Goodnight Punpun is yet another side of Asano that we haven't really seen in his previous English-language releases. While the subject matter of this series isn't that different from young-protagonist-growing-up scenarios we find in Solanin and A Girl on the Shore, the tone is much more humorous, and explicitly so. The fact that the titular character is represented as a cartoonish bird-like thing tells you something about the tone of the series. And there are many parts where the situations and characterizations are wild and psychedelic, very trippy in places. My favorite parts of this style are with hipster god figure that visits Punpun every now and again. We discussed this on a recent episode of the manga podcast, <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://comicsalternative.com/manga-reviews-girl-shore-goodnight-punpun-vol-1/">http://comicsalternative.com/manga-re...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="7541022418755521800" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1589527279" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1589527279" />
    <a title="Nicola Mansfield" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1682713-nicola-mansfield"><img alt="Nicola Mansfield" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1510729582p2/1682713.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1589527279?book_show_action=true">Mar 24, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nicola Mansfield" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nicola Mansfield" href="/user/show/1682713-nicola-mansfield">Nicola Mansfield</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1589527279" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7295465506447441544">I don't know. I was expecting something racier for a start. This is an angst-ridden coming of age story that takes Punpun through approx. two years of his life starting with his father nearly killing his mother in a domestic dispute, spending time with his uncle while father is in jail and mother in hospital, his sexual awareness, first wet dream, first girlfriend, usual kid experiences and some not-so-usual weird experiences along the way. Pretty deep with a lot of existential thinking. I think</span>
  <span id="freeText7295465506447441544" style="display:none">I don't know. I was expecting something racier for a start. This is an angst-ridden coming of age story that takes Punpun through approx. two years of his life starting with his father nearly killing his mother in a domestic dispute, spending time with his uncle while father is in jail and mother in hospital, his sexual awareness, first wet dream, first girlfriend, usual kid experiences and some not-so-usual weird experiences along the way. Pretty deep with a lot of existential thinking. I think I liked it but the fact that Punpun was drawn as a cartoon character (a bird?) and didn't even speak for the first two/thirds of the book really played havoc with my taking the work seriously. Punpun's entire family is portrayed as bird's but the rest of them speak properly. I don't know. I'm prepared to read the next volume and will see if it manages to hook me or not.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7295465506447441544" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1952130152" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1952130152" />
    <a title="Tom Ewing" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/37865461-tom-ewing"><img alt="Tom Ewing" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1418384318p2/37865461.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1952130152?book_show_action=true">Mar 26, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tom Ewing" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tom Ewing" href="/user/show/37865461-tom-ewing">Tom Ewing</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1952130152" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18276520763512966833">Bleak, funny and excruciating in turns, Inio Asano's coming-of-age manga follows protagonist Punpun through his penultimate year of elementary school. Punpun is anxious, somewhat passive but loyal and imaginative. But shyness, a chaotic home life and simple bad luck combine to make awkward situations invariably worse.<br/><br/>Obviously, the first thing you notice about Punpun is that he and his family are drawn as doodled cartoon birds, while everything else in the comic is rendered realistically. (There</span>
  <span id="freeText18276520763512966833" style="display:none">Bleak, funny and excruciating in turns, Inio Asano's coming-of-age manga follows protagonist Punpun through his penultimate year of elementary school. Punpun is anxious, somewhat passive but loyal and imaginative. But shyness, a chaotic home life and simple bad luck combine to make awkward situations invariably worse.<br /><br />Obviously, the first thing you notice about Punpun is that he and his family are drawn as doodled cartoon birds, while everything else in the comic is rendered realistically. (There's no sense that other characters perceive Punpun as anything other than human). Asano gets Punpun's emotional state across by a using a marvellous bag of cartooning tricks (close ups, shaky lines, and copy-and-paste, to name only a few) juxtaposed with the rest of the world's more standard storytelling. The result is a character whose alienation comes graphically across even as we sympathise strongly with him, and a style that captures a protagonist's interior life with often hilarious clarity. Strongly recommended if you're looking for something a little more acerbic in your manga.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18276520763512966833" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2295910220" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2295910220" />
    <a title="David Turko" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32625867-david-turko"><img alt="David Turko" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1535296189p2/32625867.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2295910220?book_show_action=true">Mar 04, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="David Turko" class="user" itemprop="url" name="David Turko" href="/user/show/32625867-david-turko">David Turko</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2295910220" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18263074073226063154">The perfect mixture of absurdity and growing up. Everything in this is beautiful. The art is probably the most impressive I've seen in a manga. The writing is borderline crazy. In between these heartfelt moments, whacky things come up like the main character talking to god or a lawyer playing hide and seek. It makes no sense and I know it'll turn several people away. But if you stick with it, I guarantee you'll read a fantastic existential manga. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2120443631" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14848713613009230282">Existential manga? Yes indeedy. Punpun is one hell of a quirky story that encompasses adolescent angst, love, loss, and a freakish mystery. Graphics are pretty cool too.</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('3olGqYR0nOmw0QFvw0mUiWeNGETfTmiHZdrSYrUcNrRwotsEO8n5v/+KvFAlLYssiC+E+8Yvuy+U9ZTe6sRTVA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('KdeWw7dctwF3o9ueya6Z3Ye1DIrm3J4hBW5d+CPcRZqH/AtuCOHSVzj4ZqEvyoZ4aBeQNf+9TYn0QRtEfAQgeg==')})
  }

A simples menção da palavra “samurai” basta para evocar o espírito do guerreiro, seguida por substantivos que parecem estar diretamente conectados a ela, como honra, bravura e perseverança. E, apesar de o samurai ser um combatente perfeito, protegido por sua armadura e com espada em punho, destaque em histórias de heroísmo e com a existência baseada num resoluto código de conduta, há um lado obscuro que envolve esses guerreiros e desafia tudo o que pensávamos saber sobre eles! Em um determinado período do xogunato no Japão, as lutas travadas nos territórios em conflito começaram a ser negociadas e ganharam contornos econômicos, quando honra, tradição e glória foram substituídas pelo comércio puro e simples. Por meio de uma barganha firmada após o resultado de um combate de espadas, o derrotado podia manter a cabeça sobre o pescoço... Desde que pagasse a quantia certa para tanto! Em O Preço da Desonra, Hiroshi Hirata explora essa questão em sete histórias ao mesmo tempo fascinantes e cruéis, capazes de transformar nossas percepções a respeito da mítica figura do samurai, e apresenta um dos seus maiores personagens, o tomador de promissórias Hanshiro.       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/685523.Inio_Asano">About Inio Asano</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/685523.Inio_Asano"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1251221178p3/685523.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/685523.Inio_Asano">Inio Asano
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
1,197
followers

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer6168776658175389194">Inio Asano (<a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/10817895._____' title='浅野いにお' rel='nofollow noopener'>浅野いにお</a> Asano Inio, born September 22, 1980 in Ishioka, Ibaraki Prefecture, Japan) is a Japanese manga author. Asano created the acclaimed manga Solanin which was released as a feature film in Japan in April 2010, starring Aoi Miyazaki. He is known for his character driven, realist stories that range from slice of life stories to psychological horror. In 2001 he won the first prize in th</span>
  <span id="freeText6168776658175389194" style="display:none">Inio Asano (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/10817895._____" title="浅野いにお" rel="nofollow noopener">浅野いにお</a> Asano Inio, born September 22, 1980 in Ishioka, Ibaraki Prefecture, Japan) is a Japanese manga author. Asano created the acclaimed manga Solanin which was released as a feature film in Japan in April 2010, starring Aoi Miyazaki. He is known for his character driven, realist stories that range from slice of life stories to psychological horror.
